					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Sotho-Tswana language spoken in South Africa</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the northeastern South African language. For the Lesotho and central South African language, see <a href="/wiki/Sotho_language" title="Sotho language">Sotho language</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>

</div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; line-height: 1.2em; padding: .1em 0;">Standard forms</div></th><td class="infobox-data" style="line-height:1.3em;"><a href="/wiki/Pedi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedi language"> Pedi</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="white-space:nowrap;padding-right:0.65em;"><div style="display: inline-block; <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"><table class="infobox" style="background:#fff6d9"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above">Sotho</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#fee8ab">Person</th><td class="infobox-data">Mopedi</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#fee8ab">People</th><td class="infobox-data">Bapedi</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label" style="background:#fee8ab">Language</th><td class="infobox-data">Sepedi</td></tr></tbody></table>

codecs=&quot;vp8, vorbis&quot;" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="640" data-height="360" /></video></span><figcaption>A speaker of the Northern Sotho language</figcaption></figure>
<p><b>Sepedi</b>, formerly called <i><b>Sesotho sa Lebowa</b></i> as an official language for the Lebowa <a href="/wiki/Bantustan" title="Bantustan">homeland</a> during <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, is a <a href="/wiki/Sotho%E2%80%93Tswana_languages" title="Sotho–Tswana languages">Sotho-Tswana language</a> group spoken in the northeastern provinces of <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a>. It is commonly referred to in its standardized form<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> as <b>Pedi</b> or <b>Sepedi</b> and holds the status of an official language in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>According to the <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Census_of_2011" class="mw-redirect" title="South African National Census of 2011">South African National Census of 2011</a>, it is the <a href="/wiki/First_language" title="First language">first language</a> of over 4.6 million (9.1%) people, making it the 5th most spoken language in South Africa. The Sepedi language is spoken most commonly in <a href="/wiki/Mpumalanga" title="Mpumalanga">Mpumalanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gauteng" title="Gauteng">Gauteng</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Limpopo" title="Limpopo">Limpopo</a> provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_Language_Status">Official Language Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Official Language Status"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sepedi_vs_Northern_Sotho">Sepedi vs Northern Sotho</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Sepedi vs Northern Sotho"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to Chapter 1, Section 6 of the South African Constitution, Sepedi is one of South Africa's 12 official languages.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> There has been significant debate about whether Northern Sotho should be used instead of Pedi.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The English version of the South African Constitution lists Sepedi as an official language, while the Sepedi or Northern Sotho version of the Constitution of South Africa lists Sesotho sa Lebowa as an official South African language.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="South_Africa.27s_Official_Language_Policy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="South_Africa's_Official_Language_Policy">South Africa's Official Language Policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: South Africa&#039;s Official Language Policy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>South Africa's English Language policy refers to the eleven official languages of South Africa as
</p><p>specified in the Constitution of the Republic of South Africa:<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.gov.za/sites/default/files/gcis_document/202011/43860gon1160.pdf">[1]</a>
</p><p>(i.e., Sepedi, Sesotho, Setswana, siSwati, Tshivenda, Xitsonga, Afrikaans, isiNdebele, isiXhosa, isiZulu, and English).
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Name"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1097763485">.mw-parser-output .ambox{border:1px solid #a2a9b1;border-left:10px solid #36c;background-color:#fbfbfb;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .mbox-text-span{margin-left:23px!important}@media(min-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .ambox{margin:0 10%}}</style><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">February 2023</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The Northern Sotho written language was based largely on the Sepedi dialect.  Missionaries studied this dialect the most closely and first developed the orthography in 1860 by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Merensky" title="Alexander Merensky">Alexander Merensky</a>, Grutzner, and Gerlachshoop.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>  This subsequently provided a common writing system for 20 or more varieties of the Sotho-Tswana languages spoken in the former Transvaal, and also helped lead to "Sepedi" being used as the umbrella term for the entire language family.  However, there are objections to this synecdoche by other Northern Sotho dialect speakers, such as speakers of <a href="/wiki/Modjadji" class="mw-redirect" title="Modjadji">Modjadji's</a> <a href="/wiki/Lobedu_people" title="Lobedu people">Lobedu</a> dialect.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_varieties_of_Northern_Sotho">Other varieties of Northern Sotho</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Other varieties of Northern Sotho"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Northern Sotho can be subdivided into <a href="/wiki/Highveld" title="Highveld">Highveld</a>-Sotho, which consists of comparatively recent immigrants mostly from the west and southwest parts of South Africa, and <a href="/wiki/Veld" title="Veld">Lowveld</a>-Sotho, which consists of a combination of immigrants from the north of South Africa and Sotho inhabitants of longer standing. Like other Sotho-Tswana people, their languages are named after totemic animals and, sometimes, by alternating or combining these with the names of famous chiefs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:No_original_research" title="Wikipedia:No original research"><span title="The material near this tag possibly contains original research. (October 2019)">original research?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Highveld-Sotho">The Highveld-Sotho</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: The Highveld-Sotho"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The group consists of the following dialects:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bapedi" class="mw-redirect" title="Bapedi">Bapedi</a>
<ul><li>Bapedi Marota (in the narrower sense)</li>
<li>Marota Mamone</li>
<li>Marota Mohlaletsi</li>
<li>Batau Bapedi (Matlebjane, Masemola, Marishane, Batau ba Manganeng - Nkadimeng Kgaphola, Nchabeleng, Mogashoa, Phaahla, Sloane, Mashegoana, Mphanama)</li></ul></li>
<li>Phokwane</li>
<li>Bakone
<ul><li>Kone (Ga-Matlala)</li>
<li>Dikgale</li></ul></li>
<li>Baphuthi</li>
<li>Baroka</li>
<li>Bakgaga (Mphahlele, Maake, and Mothapo)</li>
<li>Chuene</li>
<li>Mathabatha</li>
<li>Maserumule</li>
<li>Tlou (Ga-Molepo)</li>
<li>Thobejane (Ga-Mafefe)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Batlokwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Batlokwa">Batlokwa</a>,
<ul><li>Batlokwa Ba Lethebe</li></ul></li>
<li>Makgoba</li>
<li>Batlou</li>
<li>Bahananwa (Ga-Mmalebogo)</li>
<li>Moremi</li>
<li>Motlhatlhana</li>
<li>Babirwa</li>
<li>Mmamabolo</li>
<li>Bamongatane</li>
<li>Bakwena ba Moletjie (Moloto)</li>
<li>Batlhaloga</li>
<li>Bahwaduba, BaGaMagale, and many others</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Lowveld-Sotho">The Lowveld-Sotho</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The Lowveld-Sotho"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The group consists of <a href="/wiki/Lobedu_people" title="Lobedu people">Lobedu</a>, Narene, Phalaborwa (Malatji), Mogoboya, Kone, Kgaga, <a href="/wiki/MaPulana" class="mw-redirect" title="MaPulana">Pulana</a>, Pai, Ramafalo, Mohale and Kutswe.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Classification">Classification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Classification"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Northern Sotho is one of the <a href="/wiki/Sotho_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Sotho languages">Sotho languages</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a> family. Although Northern Sotho shares the name <i>Sotho</i> with <a href="/wiki/Southern_Sotho" class="mw-redirect" title="Southern Sotho">Southern Sotho</a>, the two groups have less in common with each other than they do with Setswana.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Northern Sotho is also closely related to <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Setswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/SheKgalagari" class="mw-redirect" title="SheKgalagari">sheKgalagari</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lozi_language" title="Lozi language">siLozi</a>. It is a standardized dialect, amalgamating several distinct varieties or dialects. Northern Sotho is also spoken by the Mohlala people.
</p><p>Most Khelobedu speakers only learn to speak Sepedi at school, such that Sepedi is only their second or third language. Khelobedu is a written language. Lobedu is spoken by a majority of people in the Greater Tzaneen, Greater Letaba, and BaPhalaborwa municipalities, and a minority in Greater Giyani municipality, as well as in the <a href="/wiki/Limpopo" title="Limpopo">Limpopo</a> Province and <a href="/wiki/Tembisa" class="mw-redirect" title="Tembisa">Tembisa</a> township in <a href="/wiki/Gauteng" title="Gauteng">Gauteng</a>. Its speakers are known as the <a href="/wiki/Balobedu" class="mw-redirect" title="Balobedu">Balobedu</a>.
</p><p>Sepulana (<span title="Northern Sotho-language romanization"><span style="font-style: normal" lang="nso-Latn">also sePulane</span></span>) exists in unwritten form and forms part of the standard Northern Sotho. Sepulana is spoken in <a href="/wiki/Bushbuckridge" title="Bushbuckridge">Bushbuckridge</a> area by the <a href="/wiki/MaPulana" class="mw-redirect" title="MaPulana">MaPulana</a> people.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">Writing system</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Writing system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Sepedi is written in the Latin alphabet. The letter <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%A0" title="Š">š</a></i> is used to represent the sound [<span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ʃ</span>] ("sh" is used in the trigraph "tsh" to represent an aspirated <i>ts</i> sound). The <a href="/wiki/Circumflex" title="Circumflex">circumflex accent</a> can be added to the letters e and o to distinguish their different sounds, but it is mostly used in language reference books. Some word prefixes, especially in verbs, are written separately from the stem.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">Phonology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Phonology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<p>Within nasal consonant compounds, the first nasal consonant sound is recognized as syllabic. Words such as <i>nthuše</i> "help me", are pronounced as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[n̩tʰuʃe]</span>. /n/ can also be pronounced as <span class="IPA nowrap" lang="und-Latn-fonipa" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span> following a velar consonant.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Urban varieties of Northern Sotho, such as <a href="/wiki/Pretoria_Sotho" title="Pretoria Sotho">Pretoria Sotho</a> (actually a derivative of <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Tswana</a>), have acquired <a href="/wiki/Click_consonant" title="Click consonant">clicks</a> in an ongoing process of such sounds spreading from <a href="/wiki/Nguni_languages" title="Nguni languages">Nguni languages</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">Vocabulary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Vocabulary"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Some examples of Sepedi words and phrases:
</p>

</th>
<th>Sepedi
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td>Welcome</td>
<td>Kamogelo (noun) / Amogela (verb)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Good day
</td>
<td>Dumela (singular) / Dumelang (plural) / Thobela and Re a lotšha (to elders)
</td></tr>

<td>O kae? (singular) Le kae? (plural, also used for elders)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>I am fine</td>
<td>Ke gona.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>I am fine too, thank you</td>
<td>Le nna ke gona, ke a leboga.
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Thank you</td>
<td>Ke a leboga (I thank you) / Re a leboga (we thank you)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Good luck</td>
<td>Mahlatse
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Have a safe journey</td>
<td>O be le leeto le le bolokegilego
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>Good bye!</td>
<td>Šala gabotse (singular)/ Šalang gabotse (plural, also used for elders)(keep well) / Sepela gabotse(singular)/Sepelang gabotse (plural, also used for elders)(go well)
</td></tr>
<tr>
<td>I am looking for a job</td>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">Sample text</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_Sotho_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Sample text"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><b><a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a></b><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup></p><div style="margin-left: 1em; font-style: italic;" lang="nso" class="poem">
<p>Temana 1<br />
Batho ka moka ba belegwe ba lokologile le gona ba na le seriti sa go lekana le ditokelo. Ba filwe monagano le letswalo mme ba swanetše go swarana ka moya wa bana ba mpa.<br />
&#160;<br />
Temana 2<br />
Mang le mang o swanetše ke ditokelo le ditokologo ka moka tše go boletšwego ka tšona ka mo Boikanong bjo, ntle le kgethollo ya mohuta wo mongwe le wo mongwe bjalo ka morafe, mmala, bong, polelo, bodumedi, dipolitiki goba ka kgopolo, botšo go ya ka setšhaba goba maemo, diphahlo, matswalo goba maemo a mangwe le a mangwe.<br />
&#160;<br />
Go feta fao, ga go kgethollo yeo e swanetšego go dirwa go ya ka maemo a dipolitiki, tokelo ya boahlodi, goba maemo a ditšhabatšhaba goba lefelo leo motho a dulago go lona, goba ke naga ye e ipušago, trasete, naga ya go se ipuše goba se sengwe le se sengwe seo se ka fokotšago maemo a go ikemela ga naga ya gabo.
</p>
</div>
